   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Community of Latin American and Caribbean States
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       "CELAC" redirects here. For other uses, see
       <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Celac_(disambiguation)" title="Celac (disambiguation)">
        Celac
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Community of Latin American and Caribbean States
       </b>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Comunidad de Estados Latinoamericanos y Caribeños, CELAC
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">
         Comunidade de Estados Latino-Americanos e Caribenhos
        </span>
       </i>
       ; French:
       <i>
        <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">
         Communauté des États Latino-Américains et Caribéens
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">
         Gemeenschap van Latijns-Amerikaanse en Caraïbische Staten
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is a regional bloc of Latin American and
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       states thought out on February 23, 2010, at the
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">
        Rio Group
       </a>
       –
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">
        Caribbean Community
       </a>
       <i>
        Unity Summit
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and created on December 3, 2011, in
       <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">
        Caracas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       , with the signature of The Declaration of Caracas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It consists of 33 sovereign countries in the Americas representing roughly 600 million people. Due to the focus of the organization on Latin American and Caribbean countries, other countries and territories in the Americas, Canada and the United States, as well as the overseas territories in the Americas of
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_departments_and_territories_of_France" title="Overseas departments and territories of France">
        Overseas departments and territories of France
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">
        Dutch Caribbean
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
        Denmark
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">
        Greenland
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">
        British Overseas Territories
       </a>
       ) are not included.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         <div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
          <ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">
           <li value="1">
            Does not include
            <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">
             Barbados
            </a>
            ,
            <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
             Cuba
            </a>
            ,
            <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
             Guyana
            </a>
            ,
            <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
             Jamaica
            </a>
            and
            <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
             Suriname
            </a>
            .
           </li>
           <li value="2">
            Proposed.
           </li>
          </ol>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       CELAC is an example of a decade-long push for deeper integration within Latin America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-en.mercopress.com_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-en.mercopress.com-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       CELAC was created to deepen
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_integration" title="Latin American integration">
        Latin American integration
       </a>
       and by some to reduce the significant influence of the United States on the politics and economics of Latin America. It is seen as an alternative to the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       (OAS), the regional body that was founded by United States and 21 other Latin American nations originally as a countermeasure to potential Soviet influence in the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-en.mercopress.com_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-en.mercopress.com-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telesurtv.net_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-telesurtv.net-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       CELAC is the successor of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">
        Rio Group
       </a>
       and the
       <i>
        Latin American and Caribbean Summit on Integration and Development
       </i>
       (CALC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In July 2010, CELAC selected
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Venezuela" title="President of Venezuela">
        President of Venezuela
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">
        Hugo Chávez
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Chile" title="President of Chile">
        President of Chile
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebastián Piñera">
        Sebastián Piñera
       </a>
       , as co-chairs of the forum to draft statutes for the organization.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states">
        Member states
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Member states">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       CELAC comprises 33 countries, speaking five different languages:
      </p>
      <p>
       Eighteen Spanish-speaking countries (56% of the area, 63% of the population)

       One
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       -speaking country (42% of the area, 34% of the population)
      </p>

         </a>

      <p>
       Twelve English-speaking countries (1.3% of the area, 1.1% of the population)
      </p>

       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>

       -speaking country (0.8% of the area, 0.1% of the population)
      </p>

       <li>
        <span class="flagicon">

      <p>
       Twelve countries are in South America, which accounts for 87% of the area and 68% of the population.
      </p>

          </a>

         A clickable
         <a href="/wiki/Euler_diagram" title="Euler diagram">
          Euler diagram
         </a>
         showing the relationships between various multinational organisations in the Americas.
         <span style="float:right; font-weight:normal; font-size:xx-small;">
          <a href="/wiki/Template:Supranational_American_Bodies" title="Template:Supranational American Bodies">
           <span title="View this template">
            v
           </span>
          </a>
          •
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Supranational_American_Bodies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Template talk:Supranational American Bodies (page does not exist)">
           <span title="Discuss this template">
            d
           </span>
          </a>
          •
          <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Supranational_American_Bodies&amp;action=edit">
           <span style=";" title="Edit this template">
            e
           </span>
          </a>
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On February 23, 2010, Latin American leaders at the 23rd
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">
        Rio Group
       </a>
       summit in
       <a href="/wiki/Playa_del_Carmen" title="Playa del Carmen">
        Playa del Carmen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Quintana_Roo" title="Quintana Roo">
        Quintana Roo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       , said they were forming an organisation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American" title="Latin American">
        Latin American
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       states. Once its charter was developed, the group was formally established in July 2011, at a summit in
       <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">
        Caracas
       </a>
       . The bloc will be the main forum for political dialogue for the area, without the United States or Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prominent left-wing leaders in the bloc praised the founding of the organization as a step towards separating Latin America from the United States with
       <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
        Evo Morales
       </a>
       , President of Bolivia saying "A union of Latin American countries is the weapon against imperialism. It is necessary to create a regional body that excludes the United States and Canada. ... it is the best time for prime ministers of Latin America and the Caribbean to gestate this great new organization without the United States to free our peoples in Latin America and the Caribbean."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telesurtv.net_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-telesurtv.net-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">
        Hugo Chávez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">
        Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva
       </a>
       , and Rafael Correa were among the other prominent left-wing leaders who praised the creation of CELAC
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction">
        Reaction
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reaction">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The announcement prompted debate and discussion across Latin America and the Caribbean about whether it was more beneficial to have close ties with U.S. and Canada or to work independently.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rueda_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rueda-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ptv-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Raúl Zibechi, writing for Mexico's center-left
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Jornada" title="La Jornada">
         La Jornada
        </a>
       </i>
       newspaper said, "The creation of the Community of Latin American and Caribbean States is part of a global and continental shift, characterized by the decline of U.S. hegemony and the rise of a group of regional blocs that form part of the new global balance."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An editorial in Brazil's conservative
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/O_Estado_de_S._Paulo" title="O Estado de S. Paulo">
         Estadão
        </a>
       </i>
       newspaper said, "CELAC reflects the disorientation of the region's governments in relation to its problematic environment and its lack of foreign policy direction, locked as it is into the illusion that snubbing the United States will do for Latin American integration what 200 years of history failed to do."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As the first summit was underway in December 2011 United States President Barack Obama's senior adviser on Latin America, Daniel Restrepo, informed reporters from Miami that the U.S. government would "watch and see what direction CELAC takes".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        </a>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_summit">
        First summit
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First summit">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1352" data-file-width="2531" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg/220px-ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg/330px-ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg/440px-ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ESO_exhibition_area_at_the_CELAC%E2%80%93EU_summit_in_Santiago.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         ESO exhibition area at the CELAC–EU summit in Santiago.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
          <a href="#cite_note-31">
           [31]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       CELAC's inaugural summit was due to be held in mid-2011, but was postponed because of the ill-health of
       <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">
        Hugo Chávez
       </a>
       , president of the host nation, Venezuela. The summit was instead held on December 2 and 3, 2011 in
       <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">
        Caracas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It primarily focused on the global economic crisis and its effects on the region. Several leaders, including presidents
       <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">
        Cristina Fernández de Kirchner
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">
        Dilma Rousseff
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">
        Juan Manuel Santos
       </a>
       , encouraged an increase in regional trade, economic development, and further economic cooperation among members in order to defend their growing economies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rueda_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-rueda-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ptv-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Chavez, and other leaders such as
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">
        Rafael Correa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">
        Daniel Ortega
       </a>
       , expressed hope that the bloc would work to further
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_integration" title="Latin American integration">
        Latin American integration
       </a>
       , end U.S. hegemony and consolidate control over regional affairs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rueda_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-rueda-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chavez, citing the
       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">
        Monroe Doctrine
       </a>
       as the original confirmation of U.S. interference in the region, openly called for CELAC to replace the OAS: "As the years go by, CELAC is going to leave behind the old and worn-out OAS."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ptv-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Correa called for a new human rights commission to replace the
       <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="Inter-American Commission on Human Rights">
        Inter-American Commission on Human Rights
       </a>
       . Other leaders argued that the organisation should be used as a tool to resolve regional disagreements and uphold democratic values, but not as a replacement of the OAS.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rueda_20-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-rueda-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptv_21-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ptv-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Santos stated that he would like to see dialogue within the group over whether existing counter-drug regulations should be revised.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rueda_20-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-rueda-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The president of the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Parliament" title="Latin American Parliament">
        Latin American Parliament
       </a>
       (Parlatino) said he expects that Parlatino will become the main legislative institution of CELAC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Amongst the key issues on the agenda were the creation of a "new financial architecture," sanction for maintaining the legal status of
       <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">
        coca
       </a>
       in Bolivia and the rejection of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_embargo" title="Cuban embargo">
        Cuban embargo
       </a>
       by the U.S.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="2013_Summit_.E2.80.93_Chile">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2013_Summit_–_Chile">
        2013 Summit – Chile
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013 Summit – Chile">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/EU-LAC_Foundation" title="EU-LAC Foundation">
        EU-LAC
       </a>
       chose CELAC to be the main organization representative of the relationship between European and Latin American and Caribbean countries. Therefore, the EU-LAC is now called the EU-CELAC.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Summit-_Cuba">
        2014 Summit- Cuba
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014 Summit- Cuba">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       During the summit, the region was declared a "peace zone". After three days and with the approval of participating representatives, a document with 83 focus points was created. It emphasized that, despite cultural and regional differences, unity between the participating countries is necessary in order to create progress. "Unity and the integration of our region must be gradually constructed, with flexibility, with respect to differences, diversity, and the sovereign right of each of our countries to choose our own forms of political and economic organization" stated the document. It also states which countries have been developing the best and how they are doing it in order for them to be a model for other countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       The issue of poverty was widely discussed. Cuba's Raul Castro pointing out that throughout Latin America and the Caribbean, people want a fairer distribution of wealth, access to affordable education, employment, better salaries, and the eradication of illiteracy. He argued that CELAC countries can work together, support each other, to create new plans and solutions for these problems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Summit-_Costa_Rica">
        2015 Summit- Costa Rica
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015 Summit- Costa Rica">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Countries discussed plans to eradicate hunger by 2025. Venezuela would host a follow up meeting in late 2015 to review the United Nations Food and Agricultural Organizations plan for their region. They called for the U.S to stop meddling in regional affairs, for Puerto Rico to be able to participate in future summits, and for the embargo against Cuba to be lifted. Statements in support of Cuba and Venezuela were widely heard. CELAC rejected U.S. sanctions against Venezuela. It was decided that a monument would be built in memory of victims of the slave trade. Member countries also supported Argentina's right to the Falkland Islands and peace negotiations in Colombia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Indicators">
        Indicators
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The following table shows various data for CELAC member states, including area, population, economic output and income inequality, as well as various composite indices, including human development, viability of the state, rule of law, perception of corruption, economic freedom, state of peace, freedom of the press and democratic level.

         <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">
          quartile
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width:3em;background:#FEFD65;">
        </td>
        <td>
         Upper-mid (3rd
         <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">
          quartile
         </a>
         )
        </td>
        <td style="width:3em;background:#FECB98;">
        </td>
        <td>
         Lower-mid (2nd
         <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">
          quartile
         </a>
         )
        </td>
        <td style="width:3em;background:#FF9865;">
        </td>
        <td>
         Lowest
         <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">

United and integrated the countries of CELAC can be powerful, "together [the 33 nations of CELAC] are the number one food exporter on the planet," further commented Ambassador Febres.
